  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8d681999-e401-45b7-ab23-4b9ac7268239'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText9747982843057926133" style="display:none"><i>Passage</i>, n.<br />i. A brief section of music composed of a series of notes and flourishes.<br />ii. A journey by water; a voyage.<br />iii. The transition from one place to another, across space and time.<br /><br />In one devastating night, violin prodigy Etta Spencer loses everything she knows and loves. Thrust into an unfamiliar world by a stranger with a dangerous agenda, Etta is certain of only one thing: she has traveled not just miles but years from home. And she’s inherited a legacy she knows nothing about from a family whose existence she’s never heard of. Until now.<br /><br />Nicholas Carter is content with his life at sea, free from the Ironwoods—a powerful family in the colonies—and the servitude he’s known at their hands. But with the arrival of an unusual passenger on his ship comes the insistent pull of the past that he can’t escape and the family that won’t let him go so easily. Now the Ironwoods are searching for a stolen object of untold value, one they believe only Etta, Nicholas’ passenger, can find. In order to protect her, he must ensure she brings it back to them—whether she wants to or not.<br /><br />Together, Etta and Nicholas embark on a perilous journey across centuries and continents, piecing together clues left behind by the traveler who will do anything to keep the object out of the Ironwoods’ grasp. But as they get closer to the truth of their search, and the deadly game the Ironwoods are playing, treacherous forces threaten to separate Etta not only from Nicholas but from her path home... forever.<br /><br /><i>Alternate cover for this ISBN can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28525008-passenger" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9747982843057926133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1063737462" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1063737462" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1063737462?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1063737462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7878114590541284672">I will write a review for this book, but really I can sum it up in two words: <b>hard work</b>.<br/><br/>Very long, very slow, very boring. Literally the only thing I liked about this book was that the male love interest was African American (because that is sadly still way too uncommon). But it was at least 150 pages too long - and I'm not sure cutting the length could liven up the pace - and very easy to put down. If I had not been reading an ARC and also didn't want to get harassed by Bracken fans for writing</span>
  <span id="freeText7878114590541284672" style="display:none">I will write a review for this book, but really I can sum it up in two words: <b>hard work</b>.<br /><br />Very long, very slow, very boring. Literally the only thing I liked about this book was that the male love interest was African American (because that is sadly still way too uncommon). But it was at least 150 pages too long - and I'm not sure cutting the length could liven up the pace - and very easy to put down. If I had not been reading an ARC and also didn't want to get harassed by Bracken fans for writing a DNF review, there is no way I would have made myself suffer through this.<br /><br />I didn't love Bracken's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10576365.The_Darkest_Minds__The_Darkest_Minds___1_" title="The Darkest Minds (The Darkest Minds, #1) by Alexandra Bracken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Darkest Minds</a> - truth be told, I thought that got really slow too once they escaped - but time travel and pirates was a premise worthy of a second chance. However, my issues started straight away with the writing style. There was something so <b>formal and distant about the third-person narrative</b>. It lacked any warmth or personality to help me connect with the characters or truly get sucked into the story.<br /><br />There are many lengthy passages full of clothing descriptions and repeated introspection. The first part of the book goes on and on about violins and compositions, the next part is all about sailing, then we finally got to the time travel and I was already falling sleep. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>The Chaconne was considered by most, including herself, to be one of the most difficult violin pieces to master--a single progression repeated in dozens of dizzying, complex variations. It was emotionally powerful, and structurally near perfect.<br /><br />His clothes were well-worn, rumpled from days of work and travel, and he seemed unbothered by it even as Sophia fussed with the gown and beat the road dust from the skirt. She had patted on more perfume of some kind, but Etta focused on the scent of him - it was cool breezes and sunshine and rum.</i>
</blockquote><br />Honestly, who cares??<br /><br />All these lengthy but pointless passages added pages to the book but no depth. It's actually hard to single out individual quotes to demonstrate how so much of this book was filler, <b>small details dragged out with unnecessary description</b>.<br /><br />I wouldn't quite call the romance between Etta and Nicholas "instalove" but it is set up from Nicholas' very first moon-eyed description of Etta. It's actually pretty slow burn, but as with the romance in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10576365.The_Darkest_Minds__The_Darkest_Minds___1_" title="The Darkest Minds (The Darkest Minds, #1) by Alexandra Bracken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Darkest Minds</a>, it was completely unneeded and lacking in tension or chemistry. The author never took the time to convince me that the two of them had some spark between them, I think I was supposed to just understand that: <i>"He was a boy, she was a girl, can I make it any more obvious?"</i><br /><br />Add to this pages-long conversations of info-dump (so, so many of these) about time travel, the "families", and the characters' pasts, and you have one very dull book. Almost 500 pages of flat, dull narrative that never reached a heart-pounding climax. <br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7878114590541284672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1466046493" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1466046493" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1466046493?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1466046493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2155224438834757196"><blockquote>
  <i>If he thought he was going to grab her, he was going to get every last ounce of New York City she possessed. Etta swung her head around, searching for something sharp.</i>
</blockquote>Whoa! Whoa! Trust me when I say that this book was all sorts of surprising. You might have recalled that last week, I read Bracken's <i>Darkest Minds</i> and hated it, to say the least. I'm always willing to give the author another chance, but to be honest, I didn't have high hopes. That's not to mention the blurb being confusing and </span>
  <span id="freeText2155224438834757196" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>If he thought he was going to grab her, he was going to get every last ounce of New York City she possessed. Etta swung her head around, searching for something sharp.</i>
</blockquote>Whoa! Whoa! Trust me when I say that this book was all sorts of surprising. You might have recalled that last week, I read Bracken's <i>Darkest Minds</i> and hated it, to say the least. I'm always willing to give the author another chance, but to be honest, I didn't have high hopes. That's not to mention the blurb being confusing and long-winded as shit. And the premise involves <b>time travel</b>, which is something that's horrifying easy to fuck up in the hands of a poor writer.<br /><br />But <b>I liked this book - a lot!</b> The first chapter was slow, but it quickly drew in my interest once I met the heroine, <b>Etta.</b><br /><br />Ignore the blurb. The book is about a violinist who somehow gets pulled back in time, turns out she's a time traveler who doesn't know it. Here's what I loved about the book. <b>The main character is fucking awesome.</b> There is a very interesting relationship between the other female in the book, a strong girl in her own right. Despite the fact that they dislike each other, both girls in the book are respectable, fierce girls in their own right, and I can't tell you how few YA books have that.<blockquote>
  <i>She drew the knife up, her chest heaving, body trembling as she pressed it against the other girl’s neck. Instinct overrode logic, compassion, patience. The ugliness that poured through her veins was unfamiliar and frightening.<br /><br />Sophia stared up at her, dark eyes widening just a fraction. Then she clucked her tongue impatiently and leaned forward into the blade, until a droplet of blood welled up at the tip.<br /><br />Before Etta could stumble back, Sophia wrapped her hand around hers, pulling it back a fraction of a centimeter from her throat. Her dark eyes burned with a wild kind of approval. Like Etta had passed an unspoken test.<br /><br />Etta could feel Sophia’s pulse flutter, light and warm, as the girl drew their hands toward her own throat again, skimming the exposed flesh.<br /><br />“Here,” she said, “right here. They’ll bleed out like a stuck pig before they can squeal, and you’ll be able to get away. Remember that.”<br /><br />“They won’t expect it from you,” she continued, “and, fool that I am, I didn’t either. Good for you. I like a fighter. But it won’t do you much good against me.”</i>
</blockquote><b>GIRL POWER, YEAH!</b><br /><br />To be honest, when we met Etta for the first time, I didn't have high hopes. Etta is a pale, pale blonde. A violinist. Sheltered, with a successful mom. <b>I fully expected her to be a weak, lily-livered Mary Sue, and I was wrong.</b> She doesn't mention her own appearance, there is no declaration of "Oh, I'm so ugly, and I'm so clumsy" shit. Etta is an highly skilled violinist, dedicated to her craft. She has given up everything she loved so she could be better, and the moment that she won me over was when she exploded in anger at the insinuation that <b>she was not good enough.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“You don’t think I’m good enough, do you?”<br /><br />“No, duck, no—”<br /><br />“Don’t call me that!” Etta said, backing out of the office. “Do you realize I don’t even have a friend left? You told me I needed to focus if I wanted my debut. I gave it all up! I don’t have anything else!”<br /><br />“Etta—Henrietta,” Alice tried, but Etta was past the point of listening, of caring what either of them had to say.<br /><br />“I’m playing,” she told her instructor, “tonight, and at the debut. I don’t care what you think, or if you believe in me—I believe in myself, and there is literally nothing in this world that can keep me from playing.”</i>
</blockquote>How do you not love a girl with that kind of spirit?!<br /><br />And indeed, her spirit, and her persistence shows throughout the rest of the book. She is a fish out of water - I mean, hello, imagine being thrown back in time to 1776 - but she deals with it surprisingly well, and realistically well. She's a fighter...she doesn't give up.<blockquote>
  <i>You can do this.<br /><br />Her mom’s words floated through her mind. Etta can handle this.<br /><br />She could. She would.</i>
</blockquote>I believed her. I believed her actions, I believed her thoughts. The book - and the time traveling - felt <b>natural</b>.<br /><br />I thought the details of time travel, down to the minutiae of dress (and the fact that people seriously stank back then), was well done, and the mechanics of time travel is vague enough to not strangle itself with its own rope.<blockquote>
  <i>“The best way to explain this is to think of the timeline as a kind of…constant, roaring stream. Its path is set, but we create ripples by jumping in and out. Time corrects itself the best it can to keep later events consistent. But if a small change snowballs into a much larger one, or if a traveler’s actions are devastating enough, it can actually shift the flow of the timeline, thereby changing the shape of the future from that point on.”</i>
</blockquote>The romance is not overwhelming, furthermore, the love interest is part black; given the distinct lack of people of color within YA literature, needless to say, I approve.<br /><br />The book is not perfect. It rambles in parts, but it was well-written, and kept my interest. And the main character is really, REALLY awesome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2155224438834757196" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10527781674317045499">I really enjoyed this book! I don't think I'm quite as blown away as most people, but it was really good.<br/><br/>This book didn't really start to pick up until about 150 pages in for me, so just give it some time whenever you pick it up - it hooks you eventually.<br/><br/>WORLD BUILDING AND TIME TRAVEL WERE GREAT. I equally loved and ha</span>
  <span id="freeText10527781674317045499" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book! I don't think I'm quite as blown away as most people, but it was really good.<br /><br />This book didn't really start to pick up until about 150 pages in for me, so just give it some time whenever you pick it up - it hooks you eventually.<br /><br />WORLD BUILDING AND TIME TRAVEL WERE GREAT. All of that was fantastic and interesting and unique and well done and I loved it.<br /><br />Overall I liked the characters, though the romance was a bit much sometimes. (insta-love anyone?) I equally loved and hated it. I really love Etta a lot.<br /><br />AND THAT'S HOW IT ENDS? Okay. I really need to know what happens next.<br /><br />Overall a great and fun read, but not BLOW ME AWAY THE BEST EVER AMAZING.</span>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1409412445">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1432782147" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1432782147" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1432782147?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=sent-from-pub">sent-from-pub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=the-worst">the-worst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=unhauled">unhauled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1432782147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1763070969218016683">If you didn't like The Darkest Minds and are wondering if this is worth reading, don't read it.<br/><br/>I began this book with an open mind after not liking TDM. I was going into it blindly because the synopsis was so vague and confusing, and reading this for the first several chapters, I just noted that there's absolutely no hook. From the description to the beginning of this book, everything was totally uninteresting, I had no idea what I was going into, and I was bored with the idea because I didn't u</span>
  <span id="freeText1763070969218016683" style="display:none">If you didn't like The Darkest Minds and are wondering if this is worth reading, don't read it.<br /><br />I began this book with an open mind after not liking TDM. I was going into it blindly because the synopsis was so vague and confusing, and reading this for the first several chapters, I just noted that there's absolutely no hook. From the description to the beginning of this book, everything was totally uninteresting, I had no idea what I was going into, and I was bored with the idea because I didn't understand it. For the first 150 pages I was waiting and waiting for something to happen. By the time it did happen, everything was NOT explained well and I was now both confused, bored, and exasperated. This entire premise needed to be explained better, and between being completely bored, mostly annoyed with the generic premise, and partially confused at the action, I ended up skimming the last half of this book. This might stem partially from the fact that i'm not a fan of historical fiction, but I just hate Alexandra Bracken's writing. This book could have been half the size it actually is, which is nearly 500 pages. There's so much FLUFF in her writing. SO many rhetorical questions and other inner monologue that is completely unnecessary and just drags the pace of the book down, so much so that I did what I told myself I wouldn't do (and did for TDM series)-- skimmed all the pages for dialogue.<br /><br />I can see how other people could enjoy this, but Bracken's books just aren't for me. I almost wish I hadn't wasted the time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1763070969218016683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_896484406" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/896484406" />
    <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews"><img alt="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468898958p2/12502667.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/896484406?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews">Rachel  (APCB Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer896484406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10030524693947897273">I'm a huge fan of Bracken's first series, The Darkest Minds, so I was stoked to hear she was writing a second series. Passenger highlights all of Bracken's strong suits: strong characters, extensive history research, character-driven plot, and shippable romance and keeps readers guessing until the very end.<br/><br/>Violin prodigy, Etta Spencer, accidentally uncovers the secret society of time travelers and is thrust into a dangerous hunt to retrieve a powerful object that could change the world for the w</span>
  <span id="freeText10030524693947897273" style="display:none">I'm a huge fan of Bracken's first series, The Darkest Minds, so I was stoked to hear she was writing a second series. Passenger highlights all of Bracken's strong suits: strong characters, extensive history research, character-driven plot, and shippable romance and keeps readers guessing until the very end.<br><br>Violin prodigy, Etta Spencer, accidentally uncovers the secret society of time travelers and is thrust into a dangerous hunt to retrieve a powerful object that could change the world for the worst if fallen into the wrong hands. The most exciting part about this hunt is that it take places in various countries in various time periods. I commend Bracken for making Passenger such a thrilling on-the-run story. The research was spot-on and and the details were impeccable. I loved all the descriptions of the time periods and the settings. I always have major fangirl moments when authors incorporate historical facts into their stories.<br><br>Etta is such a strong-willed and feisty person. I love her fearlessness and her whip-smart mind. As she follows her mother's cryptic clues from place to place to find the hidden object, Etta is thrust into harrowing situations which really help build her character and growth. But she's not on this journey alone. Enter, Nicholas Carter, a freed slave-turned privateer in the late 1700s. I think I enjoyed his character a bit more than Etta because he was such an interesting and multifaceted person. Both Etta and Nick have such strong personalities that really shine through. I am pleased to see a bit of diversity in the main cast of characters and secondly I am proud to see a biracial romance represented in this story! I love the development and the slow-burn of this one. Definitely a top power couple of the year. Overall though, I love their honesty and their courage to speak their minds (and hearts) no matter what.<br><br>Bracken's writing is so eloquent and highly descriptive. Her plotting was brilliant and never too predictable. I was hooked from the beginning (haha no pun intended...) and engaged throughout, although I did feel there was a slight pacing problem in the middle. Sometimes in the frantic action sequences I got a bit confused as to what was going on. A lot of this book is clue-solving and running, but I wish the plot could have slowed down a bit for the characters (and us readers) to explore the time periods. <br><br>Time traveling is incredibly easy for an author to mess up and quite difficult for an author to do well. Thankfully Bracken's execution and extensive attention to detail in regards to time travel were both perfect. I love how she explained time travel, made it her own (a bit different), and kept it relatively simple for us to comprehend. At times though it was a bit hard to keep up with the explanation of repercussions of all the bad things that would happen if the object fell into the wrong hands. This reminds me of Interstellar or Inception at times where the plot just went a little over my head at times... But that's a me problem! <br><br>I was a bit disappointed that not much of this book takes place on ships, especially since the cover of the book has a ship on it. That along with some minor pacing and plot issues made me shave a star off. Overall this book is historically action-packed and lots of fun! I'd definitely recommend this book to Bracken fans. <br><br>-Rachel<br><br>4/29/15 <br><br>Look at this gorgeous cover!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1430331202l/20983362.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What?! Alex Bracken is writing more books?!<br><br>HECK YEAH!!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/665743.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393993870ra/8793478.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>EEEEEEEEEKK!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381372245ra/4772368.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396221754ra/9103558.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10030524693947897273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1880562498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11250585741531353819">I had absolutely no expectations going into this one and I am glad to say that I throughly enjoyed it!<br/><br/>This book was by no means perfect. At times it was a bit cliche and aspects of the plot were somewhat unoriginal. However what I loved about this book was that it allowed me to completely escape reality. I just had such a fantastic time exploring this world and falling in love with these characters that I didn't have to think about anything else. <br/><br/>Overall, this was an extremely fun read and I can</span>
  <span id="freeText11250585741531353819" style="display:none">I had absolutely no expectations going into this one and I am glad to say that I throughly enjoyed it!<br /><br />This book was by no means perfect. At times it was a bit cliche and aspects of the plot were somewhat unoriginal. However what I loved about this book was that it allowed me to completely escape reality. I just had such a fantastic time exploring this world and falling in love with these characters that I didn't have to think about anything else. <br /><br />Overall, this was an extremely fun read and I can't wait to get to the sequel! </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1637368441" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1637368441" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1637368441?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1637368441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13174809975635756317"><blockquote>
  <i>❝Love was selfish, wasn't it? It made honest men want things they had no right to. It cocooned one from the rest of the world, erased time itself, knocked away reason. It made you live in defiance of the inevitable. It made you want another's mind, body; it made you feel as if you deserved to own their heart, and carve out a place in it.❞</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I really wanted to like this one. I really did. But I knew I wouldn't because when it came out, there mixed reviews about it but even with the mixing added,</span>
  <span id="freeText13174809975635756317" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>❝Love was selfish, wasn't it? It made honest men want things they had no right to. It cocooned one from the rest of the world, erased time itself, knocked away reason. It made you live in defiance of the inevitable. It made you want another's mind, body; it made you feel as if you deserved to own their heart, and carve out a place in it.❞</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I really wanted to like this one. I really did. But I knew I wouldn't because when it came out, there mixed reviews about it but even with the mixing added, most were negative and I had mixed feelings after. It involved time traveling and I've never been a fan of time travel, so I didn't expect much. Luckily, I didn't and I was quite glad. I don't understand time traveling. It really makes everything entertaining but at the same time boring and confusing because the whole traveling just doesn't make sense to me and leaves me wandering everywhere and trying to figure out what is going on. Sometimes it frustrates me because I hate how the protagonist/s are/is going to the future or back to the past, trying to fix things or know how to make them work. <br /><br /><i>Passenger</i> just took me forever to finish and I was glad I kept it on hold for so long. I didn't want to bother picking it up and I just wanted to leave it as a DNF but I guess giving it a shot was worth it? No, not really. There was nothing interesting and nothing I enjoyed. Nothing seemed real, characters were boring, plot went back and forth due to time traveling, and I was left skimming pages over and over because I didn't care much about a lot. Or really about anything.<br /><br />I don't like judging books by its cover and unlike my friend, I didn't judge this one. I asked my friend if she wanted to read it and she straight up said <i>No I don't want to read a book with a boat on the front</i> and well of course I was upset but glad she didn't pick it up because knowing she's a fan of fantasy and high fantasy elements, I knew this wouldn't be the book for her. She likes novels where a map is set in the beginning like <i>Throne of Glass, Falling Kingdoms, Shadow and Bone, Snow like Ashes, etc.</i> <br /><br />Alex has her own writing and it really isn't made for me to read. I'm not shaming her writing and I'm not throwing hate, but I'm not a fan of it. It's different than most writers and even though that's good at times and refreshing, knowing there are authors out there that write stories a lot differently, it's told in ways where the journey isn't a fun one but a boring one where you just want to stop and put an end to it because it's nowhere near fun and entertaining. Nothing really kept me intrigued, I just wanted to finish it and that is why I skimmed through a lot over and over and didn't care, didn't bother going back to see if I missed anything interesting since, there really wasn't. The characters didn't annoy me but there was nothing interesting. I was confused in Etta's perspective a lot more since she's the one who was saved and thrown into the world of time travel after her debut. Nicholas has a different story and his is a little more entertaining since I didn't know much about him and how he got to where he was, but at the same time it was kind of boring.<br /><br />The relationship kind of had my attention and even though it was slow, I was surprised at how old Nicholas really was and was able to blend in with Etta and see some romance between them two. Nothing was realistic and like I said, everything was pretty boring. I hated Sophia since the beginning and not trusting her was a good choice. I know she's in the sequel, and I'm really not looking forward for her stupid actions and hopefully, <i>just hopefully</i>, she doesn't have her own point of views because if she does, I really won't bother buying Wayfarer and reading about Etta's journey, and seeing where Nicholas heads to. I don't care about Sophia one bit and I just really despise her. <br /><br />I don't think there will be much improvement in the sequel but I'm still not dropping all hopes down. I guess there will be history to be told and seen in the sequel since we are reunited with Alice and Rose in Passenger so hopefully, Etta will see one of them (or both) and the stories between them all will be explained and told and everything will just make sense in the end, middle, or at least the beginning. I'm probably gonna end up reading Wayfarer just because I want to see how all the time traveling works again and since it's called Wayfarer, I'm pretty sure Nicholas will be the one traveling by foot to find Etta. <br /><br />I really tried getting into this story and wanted to like it, but it just wasn't for me. Nothing was for me. But it just had me bored the whole time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13174809975635756317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781786540003" href="/book/show/29338023-passenger">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041193927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14587459908729917130"><b>**3.5-stars**</b><br/><br/><i>'You cannot fathom the distance I would travel for you.'</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566589184ra/28040817.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This high-stakes YA Scifi Adventure really took me by surprise. While I expected it to be good, I didn't know it would be <b>this good</b>. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551065306ra/27114336.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In fact, I had so much fun reading <i>Passenger</i>, I immediately picked up the second book. <br/><br/>Initially, I started this one mainly because I hadn't read a good time travel story for almost a year and it is one of my favorite Scifi-subgenres.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566589184ra/28040816.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book had nonstop action and a scavenger hunt feel, as our m</span>
  <span id="freeText14587459908729917130" style="display:none"><b>**3.5-stars**</b><br><br><i>'You cannot fathom the distance I would travel for you.'</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566589184ra/28040817.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This high-stakes YA Scifi Adventure really took me by surprise. While I expected it to be good, I didn't know it would be <b>this good</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551065306ra/27114336.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In fact, I had so much fun reading <i>Passenger</i>, I immediately picked up the second book. <br><br>Initially, I started this one mainly because I hadn't read a good time travel story for almost a year and it is one of my favorite Scifi-subgenres.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566589184ra/28040816.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book had nonstop action and a scavenger hunt feel, as our main characters, Etta and Nicholas, follow clues to a mysterious object Etta's mother had hidden for her. <br><br>Sound confusing? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444673533ra/16534033.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At times, I'll admit, I felt a little lost but I think that was due more to my mind wandering because, <b>LIFE</b>, as opposed to an actual issue with the book.<br><br>This is the first Alexandra Bracken novel I have read and I am happy she has so many other books for me to choose from. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1578672195ra/28752827.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Her writing style is very fast-paced and that action kept me flipping pages at a speed that even for me, seemed impressive. <br><br>I finished this so quickly and am just itching to get farther into <i>Wayfarer</i>. <i>Passenger</i> left off on such a cliffhanger, I can't imagine the people who read it when it first came out having to wait for the 2nd book to be released! <br><br>Literal torture and this is why I am years behind on my duologies, trilogies and series.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566589184ra/28040818.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you are looking for a super fast, engaging and lively adventure, this could be a good fit for you. <br><br>There is some light romance, but nothing too overpowering. I didn't cringe once, so that's huge. I love Nicholas, a time traveling sailor with a heart of gold and manners to match.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566293686ra/28020368.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really enjoyed Etta as well. She is a violin prodigy under a lot of pressure to perform and live up to expectations. Once she is swept up into the unexpected reality of time travel, we really see her blossom. <br><br>I thought her character was really strong and took everything in stride. At one point, she thought to herself, <i>if my mother could do this, than so can I</i>. I loved that self-assurance with just taking things as they come. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592525577ra/29670481.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She had no clue about this whole underground world her mother was a part of and she was able to adapt and assert herself. I thought it was great to see that as opposed to a heroine who just needs to be saved!</span>

<div id="review_1536854310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1536854310" />
    <a title="Taneika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika"><img alt="Taneika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564410672p2/5591031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1536854310?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taneika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taneika" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika">Taneika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1536854310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1884992699237231016">I've been tossing up whether to give this 2.5 or 3 stars as I was curious enough about certain elements to not mark this as DNF but there were a lot of other things about this book that just plain annoyed me. I ended up giving it a 2.5.<br/><br/>Passenger is about a violinist named Etta who is thrust into the secret world of time travel on the night of her debut. She must go on a risky treasure hunt across time to find a dangerous object which has the power to change the world in drastic ways if it falls </span>
  <span id="freeText1884992699237231016" style="display:none">I've been tossing up whether to give this 2.5 or 3 stars as I was curious enough about certain elements to not mark this as DNF but there were a lot of other things about this book that just plain annoyed me. I ended up giving it a 2.5.<br /><br />Passenger is about a violinist named Etta who is thrust into the secret world of time travel on the night of her debut. She must go on a risky treasure hunt across time to find a dangerous object which has the power to change the world in drastic ways if it falls into the wrong hands. There are two families of time travellers left, one of which Etta belongs to, the other is the Ironwoods. The Ironwoods are the largest family of time travellers and make all the rules.<br /><br />Passenger is told in two different perspectives from Etta and Nicholas, and in third person point of view. Our main character Etta was interesting enough, however lacked any true depth for me to consider her an amazing protagonist. Etta is a violinist with a distant mother and while I found her boring at times, she still had just enough sass and passion for me to like her and enjoy her chapters. Nicholas on the other hand. WELL. I found myself wanting to skip entire chapters whenever Nicholas popped up because I was just not interested. He is angsty for 90% of the novel, weirdly possessive (I know he’s from the 1700’s, but come on) and there isn’t much personality to him outside of thinking about how beautiful Etta is. Seriously, he goes all moon-eyed over her the minute he lays eyes on her. One thing I do love however, is the fact that he is African American and having a love interest as a POC is still way too rare in YA.<br /><br />The relationship between the characters feels forced and unrealistic. Etta and Nicholas have exactly ZERO chemistry and the reader is pretty much told “these two are going to be together” and you're just expected to take this at face value. After a while I seriously considered DNFing this because most of the plot consisted of them making out overtime one is questioning the other’s intentions or if they think the other is mad at them. Whatever. Like, I understand they’re teenagers and they just want to be all over eachother, BUT COME ON. STOP.<br /><br />The chapters were weird. One chapter was almost 50 pages long and then you’ll have a chapter that’s 5 pages?? Although I think this might’ve affected pacing a little bit, I’m not too worried, it just made it a bit of a slog and stood out to me.<br /><br />For a book that was so long, nothing happened. The time travel was okay and my intrigue about the hidden object is largely what kept me going through this entire book. I wanted to know more about how time travel works in this world and more information about the families and this secret object. If it wasn’t for that, I don’t think I would have finished this book. There are big long paragraphs full of descriptive language, a lot of it I didn’t really care for. I enjoyed the descriptions of the different places they travelled to, however I don’t need to read that a side character put on more perfume or that Nicholas smells like sunshine for the hundredth time (what does sunshine even SMELL LIKE???? - It seems like it’s a pretty word for B.O to be honest, I could be wrong though.). These descriptions would often get slapped in the middle of a really cool scene and it would completely put me off.<br /><br />I really wanted to like this book. However the badly developed characters, barely developed relationship, the pacing and the sheer amount of info dumps (seriously, there’s so many) really disappointed me. I was so hyped to read this and I found myself so bored. Other elements kept me intrigued enough to continue though and I will probably read the next instalment purely because I want to know more about the world and history.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1884992699237231016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1285249465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1285249465" />
    <a title="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland"><img alt="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560365354p2/21937982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1285249465?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" href="/user/show/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland">Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5894944202995151900">Video review to come!<br/>The concept was killer, the characters had a ton of potential, but this book really suffered from first book syndrome, symptoms being: chronic information dumps and a sloooow moving plot. It picked up a lot in the end and I really did have fun reading it, but I didn't love it as much as I had expected. I am excited to see where the series will go though!</span>

<div id="review_1541434561" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1541434561" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1541434561?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781460752043" href="/book/show/27429432-passenger">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favourite-covers">favourite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1541434561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12790724398873289349">In a few words, I <b>LOVED IT</b><br/><br/>This story pulls you in right from the start. I was so drawn in by this world and the characters and the quest. It was captivating. I felt taken along for the journey with Etta and Nicholas, like I was travelling to all these unknown times and worlds myself. <br/><br/>The slow unravelling of the story and the mystery was great, and I loved how you had a little insight into each character that other characters didn't know about. This book makes you care so completely about the cha</span>
  <span id="freeText12790724398873289349" style="display:none">In a few words, I <b>LOVED IT</b><br /><br />This story pulls you in right from the start. I was so drawn in by this world and the characters and the quest. It was captivating. I felt taken along for the journey with Etta and Nicholas, like I was travelling to all these unknown times and worlds myself. <br /><br />The slow unravelling of the story and the mystery was great, and I loved how you had a little insight into each character that other characters didn't know about. This book makes you care so completely about the characters and worry for their poor little hearts. <br /><br />Alexandra Bracken's writing draws you so in, you're so enthralled by the story and captured in the moment. Her writing was wonderful and I love her style so much. <br /><br />I loved both Etta and Nicholas in this (and I admit I kind of pictured them as Daisy Ridley and John Boyega from The Force Awakens??) Both were such captivating and charming and interesting characters. I found I wasn't bored or annoyed by either of them and instead was just really drawn into their story and lives. Etta was such an amazing, passionate young lady I just fell in love with instantly and Nicholas is so charming. Other supporting characters like Sophia and Cryus who were given less time still felt whole and Sophia especially was an interesting character. <br /><br />The time travel in this is kind of similar to the Back to the Future style which is GREAT (I love Back to the Future) and I love that it left you thinking and a little confused. Like, "ohh so if this has already happened that means future character knows because this happened to her 50 years ago even though it's only happening now in the future. " But, I mean thats one of the best things about time travel stories, to me.<br /><br />Finally <b>
  <i>that ending</i>
</b> I'm actually so, so excited to see where this goes. I really want Sophia to grow as a character -- the whole time I felt so sorry for her, really she is just a woman trying to find some agency in a time that doesn't give women any and I hope she can get to some place where she's happy or ?? something ?? And I can't wait to see where Etta has ended up. But most of all I'm intrigued by Julian possibly being alive and I really hope he and Sophia get a happy reunion.<br /><br />I wish I could be a traveller! I love history - this would be the perfect life for me. Far flung places, in far off times. <br /><br />I just loved this book so much it was such a good book LOVED IT LOVED IT LOVED IT.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12790724398873289349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Alex has woven in some delicate intricacies of history and shown how old hurts trickle up into society hundreds of years later. She manages to deal with some very important issues in a thoughtful, intriguing way.<br/>And the romance…love, love, LOVE. So much love for it!!<br/></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1433040873" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2179717278710985879">4.5 stars!! I absolutely loved Passenger. It was a super exhilirating, heart-wrenching, wonderful story. It was completely different than a lot of books I normally read and extremely refreshing and unique! I love how Alex Bracken can write something so different from The Darkest Minds, which is an absolute favorite of mine, and yet do so well with it! Passenger just proves how much of a versatile, extraordinary writer she is. The world building was phenomenal as always, and I thought she wrote a</span>
  <span id="freeText2179717278710985879" style="display:none">4.5 stars!! I absolutely loved Passenger. It was a super exhilirating, heart-wrenching, wonderful story. It was completely different than a lot of books I normally read and extremely refreshing and unique! I love how Alex Bracken can write something so different from The Darkest Minds, which is an absolute favorite of mine, and yet do so well with it! Passenger just proves how much of a versatile, extraordinary writer she is. The world building was phenomenal as always, and I thought she wrote an extremely successful time travel novel. Full review to come on my YouTube channel on the release day!<br /><br /><i>I received a free copy of this book from Disney Hyperion. I had no obligation to review this book and all opinions are my own.</i></span>

<div id="review_1070444527" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1070444527" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605042512p2/5789353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1070444527?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-romance-slow-burn">genre-romance-slow-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=diverse-characters">diverse-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=age-young-adult">age-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-historical">genre-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-time-travel">genre-time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1070444527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2240858706915723013">Pirates, historical settings and time travel! This is pretty much the entire book and I gobbled it up! From the first page, I was already hooked. Bracken's writing pulls you in and keeps you there until the very last chapter. I had no inkling as to what this book was about because I pretty much judged it from the cover, not having read the synopsis either. I'm so happy that I did that because it made me focus on other things and not how close it was to the description.<br/> <br/>As for the characters? The</span>
  <span id="freeText2240858706915723013" style="display:none">Pirates, historical settings and time travel! This is pretty much the entire book and I gobbled it up! From the first page, I was already hooked. Bracken's writing pulls you in and keeps you there until the very last chapter. I had no inkling as to what this book was about because I pretty much judged it from the cover, not having read the synopsis either. I'm so happy that I did that because it made me focus on other things and not how close it was to the description.<br /> <br />As for the characters? There's Etta who is this driven violinist but has to overcome her stage fright. She also has a mother that she's willing to do anything to please. I thought their relationship and their dynamics were interesting. Especially since they're torn apart, and Etta has to learn how to deal without her mother to help. Then there's the main love interest who is a POC! His history and his back-story were even more interesting than Etta's. Naturally I gravitated towards both of them, wanting them to get together. A free-thinking independent 21st century teenage girl with a well-mannered 1920s young boy, how the year they were born in shaped who they were and who they could be. We both get to see the story unravel from their point of views and you can see the contrast of both. They travel to different parts of history and it was so fun to read about. There's a slow burn romance with stolen glances and touches, which ends up with a lot of kissing scenes. There were a pretty cute couple if I might add. I had such fun imagining all the different eras they fell into. <br /><br />The dialogue between people is formal, such manners! And how Etta realized how young the soldiers were. She experienced history like no one else could and it was shocking to her. Culture-shock almost. I also loved how there was a focus on racism and how Etta experienced it with her own eyes. It was heart-breaking and it made me think about the past myself. Like this quote that came from a character from the 15th century:<br /><br />Isn't it fair to say that slavery has been a boon to Africans? At the very least, it breaks them of their laziness and their barbaric violence—brings them into God's flock. The work they do is fit for their capacities. (132)<br /><br />Then Nicolas (who is African American) thinks:<br /><br />"What mattered was that these beliefs had swept through the souls of everyone like a plague. Even a hundred years in the future, he knew, the roots still had not been fully pulled up from society. Wherever, whenever he went, the colour of his skin set the boundaries of what he could achieve, and there was very little—if any—recourse for finding a way around it." (132)<br /><br />Even though there were parts where the romance was too much, I never felt bored. I liked the story-line and the settings were just great fun to read about. I'm pretty sure any historical romance fan would love this book! Bracken's writing is wonderfully crafted and now I'm itching to read her Darkest Minds series!<br /><br />RATING 4/5<br /><br />QUOTES<br /><br />"It's our choices that matter in the end. Not wishes, not words, not promises." (20)<br /><br />"I don't care what you think, or if you believe in me—I believe in myself, and there is literally nothing in this world that can keep me from playing." (32) <br /><br />"I simply cannot abide the hypocrisy of fighting for a man who supposedly embodies the ideals of freedom, while at home, dozens of slaves work his land." (131)<br /><br />"People believed this trash, and they were spreading it around like it was nothing. Like they weren't even talking about humans." (137)<br /><br />"How do you fight against a mountain? How do you move it when you don't even have a shovel?<br />Maybe you don't have to move it. Maybe you have to climb it." (207)<br /><br />"Everything changes, when given enough time." (248)<br /><br />"A bad idea is better than no idea." (252)<br /><br />"What right did a man have to take the life of such a powerful creature, to prop up his own esteem?" (365)<br /><br />"I cannot help but think, it matters not who you love, but only the quality of such a love." (409)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2240858706915723013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11211641275307823423">I ended up just skimming the rest of this book. Eventually, it just dragged on. I definitely loved the concept of this book, though. I loved the time traveling and how they had to go to different years to search for an object. I also loved the characters. They were very interesting to read about. Overall, I found the plot kind of boring and very slow. </span>

<div id="review_1212278689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12627819-taylor-knight?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12627819-taylor-knight?shelf=best-books-i-read-in-2016">best-books-i-read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12627819-taylor-knight?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212278689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16473519689582970804">Oh my gosh, I loved this book so much! Everything about this book was perfect to me. <br/>The writing was so amazing. I read Alex's other book, The Darkest Minds, last year so I had a pretty good idea of her writing style but I felt like Passenger was a million times better than The Darkest Minds. I thought the main characters, Etta and Nicholas, were so well written and beautiful. And I love that Nicholas is a person of color. That to me, is one of the biggest reasons I will recommend Passenger to e</span>
  <span id="freeText16473519689582970804" style="display:none">Oh my gosh, I loved this book so much! Everything about this book was perfect to me. <br />The writing was so amazing. I read Alex's other book, The Darkest Minds, last year so I had a pretty good idea of her writing style but I felt like Passenger was a million times better than The Darkest Minds. I thought the main characters, Etta and Nicholas, were so well written and beautiful. And I love that Nicholas is a person of color. That to me, is one of the biggest reasons I will recommend Passenger to everyone. Literature, especially the Young Adult genre, is so lacking in representation of people of color and Passenger is a step in the right direction. And I absolutely fell in love with Nicholas. He such an amazing character and I thought him and Etta made such a great team. <br />I'm so insanely excited to see the growth and development of these two in the next book.<br />I loved the concept of Passenger. I don't read a lot of books with time travel but Passenger is easily the best time travel book I've read. <br />Overall, I really loved this book. Even though it's only January, I know Passenger is going to be one of my favorites from 2016. I enjoyed every aspect of this book and I can't wait for the next installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16473519689582970804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1414049776" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1414049776" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1414049776?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1414049776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14902031954708448728">Read with all my other buddy reading addicts at <a>Buddies Books & Baubles</a><br/><br/><br/>Well I finally finished. It’s not fair this book has an absolutely gorgeous cover and I really wanted to love it but I never really got carried away by the story. I actually set this book down and didn’t pick it up again for 3 weeks. That is unheard of for me.<br/><br/><b>A few of my issues are as follows. </b> <br/><br/>❶ - <b>I never connected with the characters really.</b> <br/><br/>Etta is a master violinist with stage fright who never plays the violin through the</span>
  <span id="freeText14902031954708448728" style="display:none">Read with all my other buddy reading addicts at <a>Buddies Books &amp; Baubles</a><br /><br /><br />Well I finally finished. It’s not fair this book has an absolutely gorgeous cover and I really wanted to love it but I never really got carried away by the story. I actually set this book down and didn’t pick it up again for 3 weeks. That is unheard of for me.<br /><br /><b>A few of my issues are as follows. </b> <br /><br />❶ - <b>I never connected with the characters really.</b> <br /><br />Etta is a master violinist with stage fright who never plays the violin through the entire book. Nicholas is a black man living in a time of slavery. Even though he is a free man he has had to work very hard for his place of respect on a pirate ship. Both characters have moments of likability but overall I just never connected with either deeply. This could be because the story is told in third person but most of the dialogue is in Etta’s head so I’m not sure what the purpose of having the story be in third person is.<br /><br />❷- <b>Timetravel</b><br /><br />Okay this was just not flushed out extremely well. Some people are born with an ability to be able to go through portals in time that can be opened using various notes in music in a certain combination. While I understood some of the rules of the time travel in this story some of it just didn’t make sense. Parts of it just seemed like some arbitrary rules thrown together. You can’t go back and save people, you can’t run into yourself, you can’t go beyond a certain time and half a dozen others. But for many of them there just didn’t seem to be cohesive reasons.<br /><br />❸ - <b>YA Tropes</b><br /><br />First there is the entire insta-love factor of the story, <i>well at least it isn’t a love triangle</i>. Etta and Nicholas just met but boom sparks fly and all that. It was maybe supposed to be a more complicated love story since his is black and she is white but I never really felt the tension of it. Nicholas spends most of his time fighting the attraction just based off social norms of his time. But Etta doesn’t really care about that so much since she is from this time. Then there is the forced we shouldn’t be together because we are from different times. It all seemed so forced and I never believed their reasoning for why things wouldn’t work out..<br /><br />❹ - <b>The Story Dragged</b><br /><br />Here we are going to places in history and it should have been exciting to be in revolutionary America and England during WWII (or it could have been WWI) but I couldn’t distinguish which it was, but I found most of it to be lacking. There was no big connect to the time. They ended up in a bomb shelter in a subway for the time in England but still no big connection to the people of what was happening in each of the time jumps. I was a bit bored through most of it.<br /><br />❺- <b>Etta’s initial motivations</b><br /><br />Okay Etta wants to get back to her own time to save Alice. Well that is all well and good but Alice is a 92 year old woman and sure she still gets around well but <i>really</i> she is ninety it is a bit of a stretch to be that desperate to save someone who is that old. Not her mother or a sibling or best friend that had their whole life to live but someone who is older than your grandmother. I just never really got it. Sure there are other reasons that crop up as the story moves along but again I just never bought into the beginning.<br /><br /><br /><b>It did get better</b><br /><br />The story did get a little better towards the middle and then again at the end. But I’m sad to say that most of the things I was the most interested in where only touched on in passing. I wanted to know more about the family war that led to there only being one family in control of the portals. I also wanted to know more about the Thorns the revolutionary group that is trying to overtake the one remaining family. Finally I wanted to get more into some of the places and times they went and why some people could travel through time while others couldn’t.<br /><br />There are some interesting developments right at the end and a semi-shocking reveal that did make me curious about the next book. Since I’m completely OCD about many series it is entirely possible that I’ll read it. But a year is a ways off and maybe I’ll forget the interest I was feeling at the end.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14902031954708448728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cYlFSVK1AJGYrt7xYXbvgcvWTRIczU2tHMxcnps6YHZv72OjoyQLYdLAXfngJ2vQVxeZWHQLjcDWT2k2h1XhIA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
